Task instruction sent to agent 
# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)

## Task

Generate a comprehensive migration guide for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0**.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Envoy codebase:
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.30/` - Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024)
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.31/` - Envoy v1.31.0 (July 2024)

## Scope

Focus specifically on the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** configuration and implementation changes. This filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses.

Your migration guide should identify and document:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Incompatible configuration or behavioral changes
2. **Deprecated Features** - Fields or modes marked for future removal
3. **New Features** - Added capabilities and configuration options
4. **Configuration Updates** - Required or recommended changes to ext_proc filter configuration
5. **Behavioral Changes** - Modifications to filter behavior or runtime semantics

## Relevant Components

The ext_proc filter is primarily located in:
- Proto definitions: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/`
- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`
- Documentation: `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`

## Deliverable

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format with the following sections:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the migration and major changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Critical incompatible changes requiring action
3. **Deprecated Features** - Features marked for deprecation with migration advice
4. **New Features** - New capabilities and how to use them
5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions for upgrading configurations
6. **Testing Recommendations** - How to validate the migration
7. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur

## Requirements

- Provide specific proto field names and types
- Include before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- Explain the motivation or benefit behind major changes
- Cite specific source files where implementations changed
- Recommend best practices for adopting new features
- Identify common migration pitfalls or edge cases

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changed proto fields and implementation files
- Search for all API modifications in the ext_proc filter
- Trace configuration usage patterns across both versions
- Look for related documentation updates

    21→// [#next-free-field: 7]
    22→message ProcessingMode {
    23→  // Control how headers and trailers are handled
    24→  enum HeaderSendMode {
    25→    // The default HeaderSendMode depends on which part of the message is being
    26→    // processed. By default, request and response headers are sent,
    27→    // while trailers are skipped.
    28→    DEFAULT = 0;
    29→
    30→    // Send the header or trailer.
    31→    SEND = 1;
    32→
    33→    // Do not send the header or trailer.
    34→    SKIP = 2;
    35→  }
    36→
    37→  // Control how the request and response bodies are handled
    38→  // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove
    39→  // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed
    40→  // to be set correctly:
    41→  // 1) STREAMED Bo

>     // Possible types from source/extensions/filters/common/expr/context.cc:
>     // - String
>     // - StringView
>     // - Map
>     // - Timestamp
>     // - Int64
>     // - Duration
>     // - Bool
>     // - Uint64
>     // - Bytes
>     //
>     // Of these, we need to handle
>     // - bool as bool
>     // - int64, uint64 as number
>     // - everything else as string via print
>     //
>     // Handling all value types here would be graceful but is not currently
>     // testable and drives down coverage %. This is not a _great_ reason to
>     // not do it; will get feedback from reviewers.

120-assistanttext-
The migration guide has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what was documented:

---

## What the Migration Guide Covers

### Breaking Changes
1. **`ImmediateResponse.body` type changed `string` → `bytes`** in `external_processor.proto:342` — requires regenerating gRPC stubs and updating server code in all languages (Go, Java, Python, etc.)
2. **`disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action` cannot coexist** — Envoy throws a startup exception if both are set to non-default values simultaneously

### Deprecated Features
1. **`disable_clear_route_cache` replaced by `route_cache_action` enum** — the boolean is still accepted in v1.31 (internally mapped to `RETAIN`) but the new three-value enum (`DEFAULT`, `CLEAR`, `RETAIN`) is the recommended API going forward, with concrete before/after config examples

### New Features
1. **Observability Mode** (`observability_mode` + new `deferred_close_timeout` field 19) — "Send and Go" fire-and-forget mode; only `STREAMED` body mode supported; streams linger for a configurable close timeout (default 5s) after request completion
2. **`route_cache_action` enum** with `DEFAULT`/`CLEAR`/`RETAIN` values providing fine-grained control over route cache invalidation
3. **gRPC sidestream flow control** via runtime flag `envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control` (on by default)
4. **Tracing context propagation** to ext_proc gRPC streams (bug fix — was missing in v1.30)

### Behavioral Changes
1. **Timeout errors now return HTTP 504** instead of 500 — affects client retry logic and monitoring
2. **Route cache clear in `DEFAULT` mode now requires a header mutation** to be present alongside `clear_route_cache: true`
3. **CEL attribute type handling**: `kInt64`/`kUint64` now correctly emit `numb
... (truncated)

  "file": {
    "content": "syntax = \"proto3\";\n\npackage envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n\nimport \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n\nimport \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\nimport \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n\nimport \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\nimport \"validate/validate.proto\";\n\noption java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\noption java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\noption java_multiple_files = true;\noption go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\noption (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 18]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 20]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n  // is received in response to request headers.\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n    // field is set in an external processor response.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response.\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n    // to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. By default, request and response headers are sent,\n    // while trailers are skipped.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Send the header or trailer.\n    SEND = 1;\n\n    // Do not send the header or trailer.\n    SKIP = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Control how the request and response bodies are handled\n  // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove\n  // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed\n  // to be set correctly:\n  // 1) STREAMED BodySendMode: header processing completes before body mutation comes back.\n  // 2) BUFFERED_PARTIAL BodySendMode: body is buffered and could be injected in different phases.\n  // 3) BUFFERED BodySendMode + SKIP HeaderSendMode: header processing (e.g., update content-length) is skipped.\n  //\n  // In Envoy's http1 codec implementation, removing content length will enable chunked transfer\n  // encoding whenever feasible. The recipient (either client or server) must be able\n  // to parse and decode the chunked transfer coding.\n  // (see `details in RFC9112 <https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc9112#section-7.1>`_).\n  //\n  // In BUFFERED BodySendMode + SEND HeaderSendMode, content length header is allowed but it is\n  // external processor's responsibility to set the content length correctly matched to the length\n  // of mutated body. If they don't match, the corresponding body mutation will be rejected and\n  // local reply will be sent with an error message.\n  enum BodySendMode {\n    // Do not send the body at all. This is the default.\n    NONE = 0;\n\n    // Stream the body to the server in pieces as they arrive at the\n    // proxy.\n    STREAMED = 1;\n\n    // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body at once.\n    // If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the\n    // downstream system will receive an error.\n    BUFFERED = 2;\n\n    // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body in one\n    // chunk. If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the body contents\n    // up to the buffer limit will be sent.\n    BUFFERED_PARTIAL = 3;\n  }\n\n  // How to handle the request header. Default is \"SEND\".\n  HeaderSendMode request_header_mode = 1 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // How to handle the response header. Default is \"SEND\".\n  HeaderSendMode response_header_mode = 2 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // How to handle the request body. Default is \"NONE\".\n  BodySendMode request_body_mode = 3 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // How do handle the response body. Default is \"NONE\".\n  BodySendMode response_body_mode = 4 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // How to handle the request trailers. Default is \"SKIP\".\n  HeaderSendMode request_trailer_mode = 5 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n\n  // How to handle the response trailers. Default is \"SKIP\".\n  HeaderSendMode response_trailer_mode = 6 [(validate.rules).enum = {defined_only: true}];\n}\n",

first-class operating mode where the filter sends all processing requests (headers, body, trailers) to the ext_proc server but does NOT pause the filter chain \u2014 it returns `Continue` immediately. Only `STREAMED` body mode is supported in this mode. The `encodeComplete()` override logs gRPC stream info when in this mode.\n\n2. **`ThreadLocalStreamManager` + `DeferredDeletableStream`**: Stream ownership has been moved from a simple `ExternalProcessorStreamPtr stream_` (unique_ptr) to a thread-local map keyed by `stream_id`. The `stream_` member in `Filter` is now a raw `ExternalProcessorStream*`. Streams are stored via `threadLocalStreamManager().store()` and removed via `.erase()`.\n\n3. **Deferred Stream Close** (`deferred_close_timeout_`): In observability mode, instead of immediately closing the gRPC stream on filter destruction, closure is deferred via a timer (default: 5000 ms) to allow in-flight messages to reach the ext_proc server before the connection drops.\n\n4. **`route_cache_action` replaces `disable_clear_route_cache`**: The old boolean `disable_clear_route_cache_` field is gone and replaced with a three-value enum `route_cache_action` (`DEFAULT`, `CLEAR`, `RETAIN`). Setting the old `disable_clear_route_cache: true` now maps to `RETAIN`. Using both fields simultaneously throws a configuration error.\n\n5. **gRPC stream open options**: `client_->start()` now passes `Http::AsyncClient::StreamOptions` including parent span, parent context (stream info), and `setBufferBodyForRetry(true)`. The signature changed: it now accepts `StreamOptions` and `decoder_callbacks_` instead of just `streamInfo()`.\n\n6. **Timeout error status code fix**: On message timeout, the immediate error response status code changed from `InternalServerError` (500) to `GatewayTimeout` (504).\n\n7. **`buildHeaderRequest()` refactored**: Header request construction was extracted from inline code into a dedicated method accepting an `observability_mode` bool, which sets `req.set_observability_mode(true)` on the proto.\n\n**`processor_state.cc` \u2014 Route cache logic overhauled:**\n\nThe old binary `disableClearRouteCache()` check is replaced with a full `switch` on `routeCacheAction()`:\n- `DEFAULT`: clears cache only if the ext_proc response sets `clear_route_cache: true` AND a header mutation is present.\n- `CLEAR`: always clears the cache when there is a header mutation, regardless of the response flag.\n- `RETAIN`: never clears the cache (equivalent to old `disable_clear_route_cache: true`), logs a stat if the response tried to clear it.\n\n**`config.h` \u2014 Minor:**\n- `virtual` removed from `createFilterFactoryFromProtoTyped` (likely a `final` override cleanup).",

With this change the destructor can be called on any thread.\n    This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag ``envoy.reloadable_features.allow_slot_destroy_on_worker_threads``\n    to ``false``.\n- area: ext_proc\n  change: |\n    Adding support for\n    :ref:`route_cache_action <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action>`.\n    It specifies the route action to be taken when an external processor response is received in response to request headers.\n- area: http2\n  change: |\n    Changes the default value of ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_oghttp2`` to ``true``. This changes the codec used for HTTP/2\n    requests and responses. This behavior can be reverted by setting the feature to ``false``.\n- area: http3\n  change: |\n    Added a happy eyeballs feature to HTTP/3 upstream, where it assuming happy eyeballs sorting results in alternating address\n    families will attempt the first v4 and v6 address before giving up on HTTP/3.  This change can be reverted by setting\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.http3_happy_eyeballs`` to ``false``.\n- area: http2\n  change: |\n    Passes HTTP/2 ``DATA`` frames through a different codec API. 53. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (ext_proc) v1.30 \u2192 v1.31\n\n## Overview\n\nEnvoy v1.31.0 (released July 19, 2024) introduces several significant changes to the External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter. The release adds two major new capabilities \u2014 **Observability Mode** and the **`route_cache_action` enum** \u2014 while also changing the HTTP timeout error response code, introducing gRPC sidestream flow control, and making a wire-level type change in the service API for `ImmediateResponse.body`.\n\nMost operators will need to update their configurations to use `route_cache_action` in place of `disable_clear_route_cache`, and should be aware that ext_proc timeout errors now return HTTP 504 instead of 500.\n\n### Summary of Major Changes\n\n| Area | Change Type | Impact |\n|------|-------------|--------|\n| `ImmediateResponse.body` type changed from `string` to `bytes` | Breaking (proto wire) | Ext_proc server implementations must update generated code |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` deprecated in favor of `route_cache_action` enum | Deprecation + behavior change | Config update recommended; cannot use both simultaneously |\n| Timeout errors now return HTTP 504 Gateway Timeout instead of 500 | Behavior change | Update client error-handling and alerting |\n| New `observability_mode` field (supersedes `async_mode`) | New feature | Optional adoption |\n| New `deferred_close_timeout` field for observability mode | New feature | Optional adoption |\n| New `route_cache_action` enum with `DEFAULT`, `CLEAR`, `RETAIN` values | New feature + deprecation | Replaces `disable_clear_route_cache` |\n| gRPC sidestream flow control via runtime flag | New feature | Enabled by default; can be disabled |\n| CEL attribute type handling changed (`kInt64`/`kUint64` replace `kNullType`/`kDouble`) | Behavior change | Affects `request_attributes`/`response_attributes` users |\n| Tracing context propagation to ext_proc gRPC streams | Bug fix / new behavior | No config change required |\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. `ImmediateResponse.body` Type Changed: `string` \u2192 `bytes`\n\n**File:** `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`, line 342\n\nThe `body` field in the `ImmediateResponse` message changed its protobuf type from `string` to `bytes`.\n\n**v1.30 proto definition:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  // The message body to return with the response.\n  string body = 3;       // <-- was string\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n**v1.31 proto definition:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1;\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  // The message body to return with the response.\n  bytes body = 3;        // <-- now bytes\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n**Impact:** Although protobuf field number 3 remains the same (wire-compatible at the encoding level), the generated code in your ext_proc server will change type. In most languages:\n\n- **Go:** The field type changes from `string` to `[]byte`. Assignment code like `resp.Body = \"error message\"` must become `resp.Body = []byte(\"error message\")`.\n- **Java:** Changes from `String` to `ByteString`. Use `ByteString.copyFromUtf8(\"error message\")`.\n- **Python:** Changes from `str` to `bytes`. Use `b\"error message\"`.\n- **C++:** Changes from `std::string` to a bytes-typed field (still `std::string` in C++ protobuf, but semantically different).\n\n**Motivation:** HTTP response bodies are arbitrary binary content, not necessarily valid UTF-8. Using `bytes` is more correct and removes ambiguity.\n\n**Action Required:** Regenerate your gRPC/protobuf client stubs from the updated `.proto` files and update any ext_proc server code that sets `ImmediateResponse.body`.\n\n---\n\n### 2. `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action` Cannot Be Set Simultaneously\n\n**File:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n\nIn v1.31, if both `disable_clear_route_cache` (set to `true`) and `route_cache_action` (set to any non-`DEFAULT` value) are present in the same `ExternalProcessor` configuration, Envoy will **throw a configuration error at startup**:\n\n```\nEnvoyException: disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time.\n```\n\n**v1.30 config (valid in v1.30, throws in v1.31 if both non-default):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN   # CONFLICT: both fields now active\n```\n\n**Action Required:** Use only one of the two fields. See the [Deprecated Features](#deprecated-features) section for the recommended migration path.\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. `disable_clear_route_cache` Deprecated in Favor of `route_cache_action`\n\n**Proto field:** `ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache` (field 11)\n**Replacement:** `ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action` (field 18, new in v1.31)\n**Files:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`, `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/processor_state.cc`\n\nThe boolean `disable_clear_route_cache` field is now annotated for future promotion to a `oneof` and is superseded by the new `route_cache_action` enum. The field still works in v1.31 but Envoy internally converts it: if `disable_clear_route_cache: true` is set, it is treated as `route_cache_action: RETAIN`.\n\nThe new `RouteCacheAction` enum provides three options:\n\n| Value | Behavior |\n|-------|----------|\n| `DEFAULT` (0) | Clear the route cache only when the ext_proc response sets `clear_route_cache: true` AND there is a header mutation in the response. This is the default. |\n| `CLEAR` (1) | Always clear the route cache whenever there is a header mutation, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` flag in the ext_proc response. |\n| `RETAIN` (2) | Never clear the route cache. Equivalent to the old `disable_clear_route_cache: true`. Increments the `clear_route_cache_disabled` stat if the response tried to clear it. |\n\nAdditionally, in v1.31 the `DEFAULT` behavior itself changed slightly: the route cache is now only cleared when **both** the ext_proc response's `clear_route_cache` field is `true` **and** there is at least one header mutation. In v1.30, any response with `clear_route_cache: true` (even without header mutations) would trigger a cache clear.\n\n**v1.30 config:**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**v1.31 recommended config (equivalent behavior):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Migration advice:**\n- Replace `disable_clear_route_cache: true` \u2192 `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- Replace `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (or omitting the field) \u2192 `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` (or omit, same result)\n- To always force a route re-computation on header mutations: use `route_cache_action: CLEAR`\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Observability Mode (`observability_mode`)\n\n**Proto field:** `ExternalProcessor.observability_mode` (field 17, existed in v1.30 but formalized in v1.31)\n**New field:** `ExternalProcessor.deferred_close_timeout` (field 19, new in v1.31)\n**Files:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`, `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h`, `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n\nObservability mode (also called \"Send and Go\" mode) allows the ext_proc filter to forward all configured processing steps to the external processor **without pausing the filter chain**. Envoy sends each message and immediately continues processing \u2014 it does not wait for a response. This is the recommended replacement for the unimplemented `async_mode` concept.\n\n**Characteristics of observability mode:**\n1. Only `STREAMED` body processing mode is supported. Other body modes (`BUFFERED`, `BUFFERED_PARTIAL`) are silently ignored. `NONE` (skip body) still works.\n2. The external processor should not send responses; any responses sent are ignored.\n3. `message_timeout` does not apply in this mode.\n4. The external processor may close the stream to signal it no longer needs data.\n5. The gRPC stream is closed **after a deferred timeout** (default: 5 seconds) rather than immediately on filter destruction, to allow in-flight messages to drain.\n\n**New `deferred_close_timeout` field:**\n\nIn v1.31, when `observability_mode` is `true`, the gRPC stream to the ext_proc server is not closed immediately when the HTTP request/response completes. Instead, it is closed after a configurable delay, giving the ext_proc server time to receive and process all buffered messages.\n\nDefault value: **5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)**\n\n**Example configuration:**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_observer_cluster\n    observability_mode: true\n    deferred_close_timeout: 10s    # Allow 10s for stream drain (default: 5s)\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n      request_body_mode: STREAMED  # Only STREAMED is supported in observability mode\n      response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n**Flow control warning:** Flow control to prevent fast senders from overwhelming a slower ext_proc server in observability mode is not yet fully implemented. Use this feature at your own discretion, especially under high traffic. (Tracked at [envoy issue #33319](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319).)\n\n---\n\n### 2. `route_cache_action` Enum\n\n**Proto field:** `ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action` (field 18)\n**File:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\nSee the [Deprecated Features](#deprecated-features) section for full details. The key new capability is `CLEAR` mode, which lets you configure ext_proc to always re-evaluate routes after header modifications, without requiring the ext_proc server to set the `clear_route_cache` flag in each response.\n\n**Example \u2014 always clear route cache:**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n    route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. gRPC Sidestream Flow Control\n\n**Runtime flag:** `envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control`\n**Files:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.h`, `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.cc`, `source/common/runtime/runtime_features.cc`\n\nv1.31 adds flow control support to the bidirectional gRPC stream between Envoy and the ext_proc server. When enabled (default: `true`), Envoy sets watermark callbacks on the gRPC stream and removes them when the stream closes, preventing the ext_proc stream from being flooded with data faster than the external server can process it.\n\nThis feature is enabled by default and requires no configuration. It can be disabled via the runtime flag if it causes issues:\n\n```yaml\n# Bootstrap config to disable (if needed)\nlayered_runtime:\n  layers:\n  - name: static_layer\n    static_layer:\n      envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control: false\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. Tracing Context Propagation to ext_proc gRPC Streams\n\n**File:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n**Changelog:** `changelogs/current.yaml` (minor behavior change)\n\nIn v1.31, tracing context headers (e.g., `traceparent`, `x-b3-traceid`) are now correctly propagated when Envoy opens the gRPC stream to the ext_proc server. In v1.30 and earlier, these headers were not set on the gRPC sidestream connection.\n\nThis change affects both the Envoy gRPC client and the Google C++ gRPC client. No configuration changes are required, but ext_proc server operators may now observe tracing headers that were previously absent. This enables distributed tracing to span the ext_proc side-channel.\n\n---\n\n### 5. New Test Infrastructure: Tracing Test Filter\n\n**Files:** `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/tracer_test_filter.cc`, `test/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/tracer_test_filter.proto` (new in v1.31)\n\nA new tracing test filter and matching utilities test (`matching_utils_test.cc`) have been added. These are test-only components and do not affect production behavior, but signal that tracing integration is now formally tested for ext_proc.\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Timeout Errors Now Return HTTP 504 Instead of HTTP 500\n\n**File:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n**Changelog:** `changelogs/current.yaml`, minor behavior change section\n\nWhen the ext_proc filter's `message_timeout` expires before the external processor responds, Envoy now sends an HTTP **504 Gateway Timeout** response to the downstream client. Previously, this error returned HTTP **500 Internal Server Error**.\n\n**Impact:**\n- Downstream clients that check for `500` errors to detect ext_proc timeout failures must now also check (or switch to checking) for `504`.\n- Alert rules and dashboards monitoring for `5xx` errors are not affected \u2014 both codes are counted as server errors.\n- The `RESPONSE_CODE_DETAILS` access log field for these errors will reflect the gateway timeout.\n\n**No configuration change is required**, but you should:\n- Update any client-side retry logic that specifically matches on HTTP 500 for ext_proc timeouts.\n- Update monitoring dashboards and SLO definitions that specifically count ext_proc-induced HTTP 500s.\n\n---\n\n### 2. Route Cache Clear Now Requires Header Mutation (DEFAULT mode)\n\n**File:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/processor_state.cc`\n\nIn v1.30, if an ext_proc response set `clear_route_cache: true`, the route cache was cleared regardless of whether the response also contained a header mutation.\n\nIn v1.31 with `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` (the default), the route cache is **only cleared when both conditions are true:**\n1. The ext_proc response sets `clear_route_cache: true`, **and**\n2. The response includes at least one header mutation (`has_header_mutation()` returns true).\n\nIf an ext_proc response sets `clear_route_cache: true` but has no header mutations, the cache clear is skipped and the `clear_route_cache_ignored` counter is incremented.\n\n**Motivation:** Clearing the route cache is only meaningful when headers have changed. A response requesting cache clear with no mutations is likely a bug in the ext_proc server.\n\n**Action Required:** If your ext_proc server sets `clear_route_cache: true` on responses without header mutations, you need to either:\n- Add a header mutation to the response (even a no-op one), or\n- Switch to `route_cache_action: CLEAR` to always clear on header mutations regardless of the flag, or\n- Fix the ext_proc server to not set `clear_route_cache` when there are no header mutations.\n\n---\n\n### 3. CEL Attribute Value Type Handling Changed\n\n**File:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/matching_utils.cc`\n\nThe CEL expression evaluation for `request_attributes` and `response_attributes` changed how it maps CEL value types to protobuf `Value` types:\n\n| CEL Type | v1.30 behavior | v1.31 behavior |\n|----------|---------------|---------------|\n| `kNullType` | Sets `null_value` in proto Value | **Removed** \u2014 no longer handled |\n| `kDouble` | Sets `number_value` via `DoubleOrDie()` | **Removed** \u2014 replaced by integer handling |\n| `kInt64` | Not explicitly handled (fell through) | Sets `number_value` via `Int64OrDie()` |\n| `kUint64` | Not explicitly handled (fell through) | Sets `number_value` via `Uint64OrDie()` |\n\n**Impact:**\n- Attributes with CEL expressions that evaluate to `null` or floating-point `double` values will no longer produce `number_value` or `null_value` fields in the `attributes` map. They will fall through to string conversion instead.\n- Attributes that evaluate to `int64` or `uint64` values now correctly appear as `number_value` in the attributes map sent to the ext_proc server.\n\nThis is primarily relevant for operators using numeric or null-returning CEL expressions in `request_attributes` or `response_attributes`.\n\n---\n\n### 4. Stream Lifecycle and `notifyFilterDestroy()`\n\n**Files:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client.h`, `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.h`, `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.cc`\n\nInternally, the gRPC stream between Envoy and the ext_proc server is now managed by a thread-local `ThreadLocalStreamManager` rather than being owned directly by the filter instance as a `unique_ptr`. The `ExternalProcessorStream` interface gained a new `notifyFilterDestroy()` method that must be called when the filter is destroyed, to prevent the stream from making callbacks into a destroyed filter object.\n\nThe `callbacks_` member in `ExternalProcessorStreamImpl` changed from a raw reference (`ExternalProcessorCallbacks&`) to an optional reference (`OptRef<ExternalProcessorCallbacks>`), which is reset to empty when `notifyFilterDestroy()` is called.\n\n**Impact on custom ext_proc client implementations:** If you have implemented a custom `ExternalProcessorClient` (unlikely for most operators, but possible for testing), you must implement the new `notifyFilterDestroy()` pure virtual method.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Update Protobuf Generated Code\n\nRe-generate your ext_proc server's gRPC stubs from the updated `.proto` files:\n\n```bash\n# Example for Go\nprotoc --go_out=. --go-grpc_out=. \\\n  api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto\n\n# Example for Java (Maven)\nmvn generate-sources\n```\n\nAfter regeneration, fix any compilation errors caused by the `ImmediateResponse.body` type change from `string` to `bytes`:\n\n**Go \u2014 before:**\n```go\nimmediateResponse := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &envoy_type.HttpStatus{Code: envoy_type.StatusCode_Forbidden},\n    Body:   \"Access denied\",  // was string\n}\n```\n\n**Go \u2014 after:**\n```go\nimmediateResponse := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &envoy_type.HttpStatus{Code: envoy_type.StatusCode_Forbidden},\n    Body:   []byte(\"Access denied\"),  // now bytes\n}\n```\n\n**Java \u2014 before:**\n```java\nImmediateResponse response = ImmediateResponse.newBuilder()\n    .setStatus(HttpStatus.newBuilder().setCode(StatusCode.Forbidden))\n    .setBody(\"Access denied\")  // was String\n    .build();\n```\n\n**Java \u2014 after:**\n```java\nImmediateResponse response = ImmediateResponse.newBuilder()\n    .setStatus(HttpStatus.newBuilder().setCode(StatusCode.Forbidden))\n    .setBody(ByteString.copyFromUtf8(\"Access denied\"))  // now ByteString\n    .build();\n```\n\n---\n\n### Step 2: Replace `disable_clear_route_cache` with `route_cache_action`\n\nSearch your Envoy configurations for `disable_clear_route_cache` and replace:\n\n```bash\n# Find all occurrences\ngrep -r \"disable_clear_route_cache\" /path/to/envoy/configs/\n```\n\nApply the following replacement mapping:\n\n| Old config | New config |\n|------------|------------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` | Remove field (or `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`) |\n| _(field absent)_ | No change needed |\n\n**Full before/after example:**\n\nBefore (v1.30):\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: my_ext_proc\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n    disable_clear_route_cache: true\n    message_timeout: 0.2s\n```\n\nAfter (v1.31):\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: my_ext_proc\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n    route_cache_action: RETAIN\n    message_timeout: 0.2s\n```\n\n---\n\n### Step 3: Update Timeout Error Handling\n\nUpdate any downstream clients, retry policies, or monitoring rules that specifically detect ext_proc timeout failures via HTTP 500:\n\n```yaml\n# Envoy retry policy \u2014 update to include 504\nretry_policy:\n  retry_on: \"gateway-error,connect-failure,retriable-4xx\"\n  # \"gateway-error\" already covers 502, 503, 504 \u2014 no change needed\n  # But if you had custom logic for 500 specifically for ext_proc, update it\n```\n\nFor custom client-side logic:\n- Before: `if response.status_code == 500 and \"ext_proc timeout\" in response.body`\n- After: `if response.status_code == 504`\n\n---\n\n### Step 4: Audit CEL Attribute Expressions\n\nIf you use `request_attributes` or `response_attributes` with CEL expressions, audit any expressions that might return:\n- `null` values (were sent as `null_value`, now fall through to string)\n- Floating-point `double` values (were sent as `number_value`, now may fall through to string)\n- Integer values (were silently dropped, now correctly sent as `number_value`)\n\nTest your ext_proc server's attribute handling with representative requests to ensure the type changes do not cause parse failures.\n\n---\n\n### Step 5: Verify Route Cache Behavior (if using `clear_route_cache`)\n\nIf your ext_proc server sets `clear_route_cache: true` in responses, verify whether it always includes at least one header mutation in those responses:\n\n1. Enable debug logging: `ENVOY_LOG_LEVEL=debug`\n2. Look for log messages: `\"NOT clearing route cache. No header mutation in the response\"` \u2014 this indicates your ext_proc server is setting `clear_route_cache: true` on responses without mutations.\n3. Monitor the `clear_route_cache_ignored` stat counter \u2014 a non-zero value indicates affected requests.\n\n---\n\n### Step 6: Optionally Adopt Observability Mode\n\nIf you previously used a workaround for async/fire-and-forget processing, evaluate adopting `observability_mode: true`. Configure a suitable `deferred_close_timeout` based on your expected processing latency:\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n- name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n  typed_config:\n    \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n    grpc_service:\n      envoy_grpc:\n        cluster_name: ext_proc_observer\n    observability_mode: true\n    deferred_close_timeout: 5s   # Tune based on your processor's latency\n    processing_mode:\n      request_header_mode: SEND\n      response_header_mode: SEND\n      request_body_mode: STREAMED    # Only STREAMED works in observability mode\n      response_body_mode: NONE       # NONE is fine too\n```\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### 1. Integration Test: `ImmediateResponse.body` Type Change\n\nWrite an integration test where your ext_proc server sends an `ImmediateResponse` with a non-empty body, and verify:\n- The downstream client receives the expected body content.\n- Non-UTF-8 binary body content is transmitted correctly (since `bytes` now allows this).\n\n### 2. Integration Test: Timeout Error Code\n\nSimulate an ext_proc server that does not respond within `message_timeout`:\n```yaml\nmessage_timeout: 0.1s  # 100ms \u2014 short enough to trigger easily in tests\n```\nVerify the downstream client receives **HTTP 504**, not HTTP 500.\n\n### 3. Unit Test: Route Cache Behavior\n\nFor each `route_cache_action` setting, test with:\n- An ext_proc response that sets `clear_route_cache: true` WITH a header mutation \u2192 cache should clear in `DEFAULT` and `CLEAR` modes.\n- An ext_proc response that sets `clear_route_cache: true` WITHOUT a header mutation \u2192 cache should NOT clear in `DEFAULT` mode; verify `clear_route_cache_ignored` stat increments.\n- `route_cache_action: RETAIN` \u2192 cache never clears; verify `clear_route_cache_disabled` stat increments when the response requests a clear.\n- `route_cache_action: CLEAR` \u2192 cache always clears when there are header mutations, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` flag.\n\n### 4. Stat Monitoring\n\nMonitor the following ext_proc stats to validate migration:\n\n| Stat | Expected behavior post-migration |\n|------|----------------------------------|\n| `ext_proc.<prefix>.clear_route_cache_disabled` | Increments when `route_cache_action: RETAIN` blocks a requested cache clear |\n| `ext_proc.<prefix>.clear_route_cache_ignored` | Increments when `DEFAULT` mode skips clearing due to no header mutations |\n| `ext_proc.<prefix>.clear_route_cache_upstream_ignored` | Increments when ext_proc is in upstream filter chain (cannot clear route cache) |\n\n### 5. Observability Mode Testing\n\nWhen testing `observability_mode`:\n- Verify that the filter chain does **not** pause at ext_proc processing points (response latency should not include ext_proc server latency).\n- Verify that your ext_proc server still receives all configured messages.\n- Test the `deferred_close_timeout` by measuring when the gRPC stream closes after the HTTP request completes.\n- Confirm that only `STREAMED` body mode messages are delivered (not `BUFFERED` or `BUFFERED_PARTIAL`).\n\n### 6. Runtime Flag Validation\n\nTest gRPC sidestream flow control behavior:\n```yaml\n# Test with flow control disabled\nlayered_runtime:\n  layers:\n  - name: static_layer\n    static_layer:\n      envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control: false\n```\nCompare behavior with it enabled (default) to confirm no regressions.\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\nIf issues arise after upgrading to v1.31, here is how to revert specific changes:\n\n### Rollback: Route Cache Action\n\nThe `route_cache_action` field is new in v1.31. If rolling back to v1.30, remove `route_cache_action` from your config and restore `disable_clear_route_cache` if you need it:\n\n```yaml\n# v1.31 config\nroute_cache_action: RETAIN\n\n# v1.30 rollback config\ndisable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\nNote: v1.30 does not know about `route_cache_action` and will **reject the config** if that field is present. Remove it before rolling back.\n\n### Rollback: Timeout Error Code (504 vs 500)\n\nThere is no runtime flag to revert to the 500 behavior. If your clients or SLOs critically depend on the 500 code, you must pin to v1.30 until they are updated.\n\n### Rollback: gRPC Sidestream Flow Control\n\nDisable the new flow control feature while remaining on v1.31:\n```yaml\nlayered_runtime:\n  layers:\n  - name: static_layer\n    static_layer:\n      envoy.reloadable_features.grpc_side_stream_flow_control: false\n```\n\n### Rollback: `ImmediateResponse.body` Type Change\n\nIf your ext_proc server's generated code cannot be updated before the rollback window closes, pin to v1.30's protobuf definitions. In most protobuf implementations, a `string` field and a `bytes` field with the same field number are wire-compatible (both encoded as length-delimited), so a v1.30 server sending a `string` body will be received correctly by v1.31 Envoy, and vice versa. However, the generated API types will mismatch and cause compilation errors, requiring code changes.\n\n### Rollback: Observability Mode\n\nIf `deferred_close_timeout` is causing streams to linger too long:\n- Decrease `deferred_close_timeout` (minimum: any positive duration).\n- Disable `observability_mode` entirely until root cause is identified.\n\n### General Rollback Procedure\n\n1. Remove any v1.31-only config fields (`route_cache_action`, `deferred_close_timeout`) before rolling back the binary.\n2. Restore `disable_clear_route_cache` if previously used.\n3. Roll back the Envoy binary to v1.30.\n4. Roll back ext_proc server generated code to v1.30 proto definitions.\n5. Verify the `clear_route_cache_ignored` stat is no longer incrementing unexpectedly.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: Changed Files Reference\n\n| File | Type of Change |\n|------|---------------|\n| `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto` | Added `RouteCacheAction` enum, `route_cache_action` field (18), `deferred_close_timeout` field (19); deprecated `disable_clear_route_cache` (annotated with `oneof_promotion`) |\n| `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto` | Changed `ImmediateResponse.body` from `string` to `bytes` |\n| `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h` | Added `ThreadLocalStreamManager`, `DeferredDeletableStream`; replaced `disable_clear_route_cache_` bool with `route_cache_action_` enum; added `observability_mode_` and `deferred_close_timeout_`; stream changed from `unique_ptr` to raw `ExternalProcessorStream*` |\n| `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc` | Constructor moved to .cc; added `deferredCloseStream()`, `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()`, `sendDataInObservabilityMode()`; fixed timeout error code 500\u2192504; added tracing context to gRPC stream options |\n| `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/processor_state.cc` | Route cache logic replaced: binary bool check replaced with `switch(routeCacheAction())`; added header-mutation-required guard for DEFAULT mode |\n| `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client.h` | Added `notifyFilterDestroy()` pure virtual method; changed `start()` signature |\n| `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.h` | Changed `callbacks_` from `ExternalProcessorCallbacks&` to `OptRef<ExternalProcessorCallbacks>`; added `grpc_side_stream_flow_control_` runtime feature flag; added `notifyFilterDestroy()` |\n| `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.cc` | Updated `start()`/`create()`/`startStream()` to use `StreamOptions`;
